  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_701beb51-454d-4402-83fe-dcc0a805d694'

  <span id="freeText15557352253589325890" style="display:none">Ruby never asked for the abilities that almost cost her her life. Now she must call upon them on a daily basis, leading dangerous missions to bring down a corrupt government and breaking into the minds of her enemies. Other kids in the Children’s League call Ruby “Leader”, but she knows what she really is: a monster. <br /><br />When Ruby is entrusted with an explosive secret, she must embark on her most dangerous mission yet: leaving the Children’s League behind. Crucial information about the disease that killed most of America’s children—and turned Ruby and the others who lived into feared and hated outcasts—has survived every attempt to destroy it. But the truth is only saved in one place: a flashdrive in the hands of Liam Stewart, the boy Ruby once believed was her future—and who now wouldn’t recognize her. <br /><br />As Ruby sets out across a desperate, lawless country to find Liam—and answers about the catastrophe that has ripped both her life and America apart—she is torn between old friends and the promise she made to serve the League. Ruby will do anything to protect the people she loves. But what if winning the war means losing herself?</span>

Vida, Jude, Nico and I liked Cate who was sort of their supervisor. I wasn't sure about Alban at fir</span>
  <span id="freeText13013338822722403389" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: 99 cents Kindle US 5/19/19</b><br><br>This book surely ended on a cliffhanger! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489506712i/22221671._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But it was more of an in your face cliffhanger =) <br><br>Ruby has joined the Children's League and the others in the first book are out on their own. I should have re-read that one first but it's all good. <br><br>Some of the older characters do make their way back into this book. Along with some new ones that Ruby has met in the League. Vida, Jude, Nico and I liked Cate who was sort of their supervisor. I wasn't sure about Alban at first but it seems he was working for the greater good. Unless of course they pulled the wool over my eyes. <br><br>Ruby goes out on OPS with different groups to try and help some other kids that have talents like she does. The kids in the book have different colored labels. Ruby is an orange and she's one of the most dangerous with red being the top one. There's this whole description about it you can read about in the first book! <br><br>Ruby can change your memories or just read your mind. Or she can kill your brain so to speak. But she's a good girl and doesn't do harm to those that aren't dangerous. <br><br>In the first book Ruby had a thing going with Liam but he is out of the picture for now because of reasons. But his brother Cole is brought into the League and then all kinds of things start happening. <br><br>Runaways, finding kids that were thought dead that are still alive, search and rescue kids, try not to die while being shot at or bombed. And then we always run into jerk kids that want to run things and be over other sweet kids and gah!!!!!!! <br><br>Oh there is a jerk kid in the League named Rob, I loathed him. You can't trust everyone. <br><br>Then toward the end a sweet person dies............................NOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431761572ra/14864982.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At the end there is a big ole revelation that I wonder if it will come to pass in the next book. I want it for the kids but . . . . lets just say I like them the way they are to a certain extent.<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/03/never-fade-by-alexandra-bracken.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423159339" href="/book/show/20454580-never-fade">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787552220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14725744728201200885"><b>3.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/>After I finished reading Never Fade, I'm quite sure that if I read this trilogy back when I was 15-17 years old (well the books weren't out yet 10 years ago so it's impossible), it would've been included into my favorite shelves and received 5 stars from me, for both books so far. However, I'm 27 now and again I should state, Never Fade still doesn't provide anything new to the genre. I've seen everything here before in movies, video games and it's still the same teenage-survivor-dyst</span>
  <span id="freeText14725744728201200885" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br />After I finished reading Never Fade, I'm quite sure that if I read this trilogy back when I was 15-17 years old (well the books weren't out yet 10 years ago so it's impossible), it would've been included into my favorite shelves and received 5 stars from me, for both books so far. However, I'm 27 now and again I should state, Never Fade still doesn't provide anything new to the genre. I've seen everything here before in movies, video games and it's still the same teenage-survivor-dystopia genre which have been done to death but at this point it's safe to say that I enjoyed reading this much more than watching Hunger Games or the disastrous Divergent series. It's probably a bit unfair to compare them since I haven't read the Hunger Games or Divergent books but I watched the movies and I don't think this time the books can redeemed the stain I have towards them, especially the Divergent series.<br /><br />Never Fade is actually better than the first book in almost every aspect and yet I decided to give a 3.5 star rating. The reason for this is because of the two cons I have on the book:<br /><br />1. There's still nothing new here.<br />2. Ruby, the main character is so irritating.<br /><br />In the first book I was so-so with how I felt about her but this time, she grew to be much more annoying and considering everything in the story is from her POV, it's quite painful to read. It's like she's in an endless PMS cycle which made her emotional as fuck in all her decisions. One moment she act like she's the strongest person with her self-called "I'm a monster, don't come near me or I'll kill you" &lt;-- not exact quote and the next second she broke down because of that strength with the same reasoning, over and over again. Sure there's a reason for this and she's a flawed heroine but it's still annoying seeing this repeating since the beginning of book 1 until now. Luckily, there's a positive outcome to be taken from this. She made all the other side characters shine bright like a diamond (yeah you can sing that Rihanna song now)<br /><br />All the side characters are well created. Liam is not as bright as he is in book 1 but after all the things he's been through from the beginning and the novella, it's really understandable why he act like he did. However, Chubs is back in full throttle and he became my favorite character so far, I still have to read book 3 to see if it will remain that way. He's the epitome of what a true friend should be, doesn't matter how young or old you are. You look at what he does and you know you should aspire to be like him in maintaining your friendship. He's realistic, not afraid to tell your mistakes straight to your face, loyal and despite all the disagreement, he will do anything to help his friends. The greatest new addition side character goes to Jude but I can't tell you anything about him since he appeared since the beginning of the book til the end and I don't want to spoil you, just know that there's a lot of humor coming from him and Chubs.<br /><br />There's more actions this time compared to before and yes, most of them occurred around the Powers the characters have. Red for Pyrokinesis, Orange for Mind Control, Blue for Telekinesis, Yellow for Electrokinesis and Green for Superb Intellectual but I find it there's still some unexplained reasoning behind how Orange's power work. Hopefully it will redeemed in book 3.<br /><br />Lastly, there's much more plot progression this time and the writing is still great as before. Seriously, I really like Bracken's writing as she managed to pull me so much into caring towards the characters she created and stories that's been overdone before. I'm almost quite sure by now that when they made the movies of this trilogy, I will dislike it cause you know the simple equation, books is always better than the movies.<br /><br />I'm closing this review with my favorite quote from the book by Ruby for you to sink in when you're having a bad day. (there's a lot of great ones by the way)<br /><br /><i>“Life isn’t fair." I said. "It’s taken me a while to get that. It’s always going to disappoint you in some way or another. You’ll make plans, and it’ll push you in another direction. You will love people, and they’ll be taken away no matter how hard you fight to keep them. You’ll try for something and won’t get it. You don’t have to find meaning in it; you don’t have to try to change things. You just have to accept the things that are out of your hands and try to take care of yourself. That’s your job.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14725744728201200885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692226861" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer28206884780858491"><blockquote>
  <i>“Sometimes you're the one speeding along in a panic, doing too much, not paying attention, wrecking things you don't mean to. And sometimes life just happens to you, and you can't dodge it. It crashes into you because it wants to see what you're made of.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book is AMAZING!!!! I could not stop reading it and there were so many things happening so I was never bored. This is really one of the best books I’ve read. Everything was perfect and the plot was so so good and throughout this whole </span>
  <span id="freeText28206884780858491" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Sometimes you're the one speeding along in a panic, doing too much, not paying attention, wrecking things you don't mean to. And sometimes life just happens to you, and you can't dodge it. It crashes into you because it wants to see what you're made of.” </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book is AMAZING!!!! I could not stop reading it and there were so many things happening so I was never bored. This is really one of the best books I’ve read. Everything was perfect and the plot was so so good and throughout this whole book when I was reading I experienced so many different emotions. This was a very big improvement compared to the first book. <i>Never Fade</i> was, even more, action packed and there were so many new characters. <br /><br />First of all, I did not expect to give this book a 5-star rating like I did with the first book because, to be honest, it took me three months to actually get into this book. I got 21% through and put it aside for a long time because I just wasn’t enjoying it that much. Before I picked this book up, on my feed there was a review by someone (I can’t remember who), they said that they didn’t enjoy the book as much as the first because they didn’t read it straight after. I was worried because I didn’t pick this book until a while after so I thought that was going to happen to me. Then when I got 21% through and didn’t continue I was even more worried that I was going to hate it but I actually ended up loving this book so much. <br /><br />There were a lot of new characters in this book. But, there wasn't only new characters but all the character from the first book changed drastically. Ruby went through a lot of character development in this book. She was stronger and had a lot more control over her abilities. This was mainly due to the League and all the training she received from them. She finally had control over her life and knew what she wanted to do. Chubs also changed immensely and so did Liam. Liam sadly wasn't in the book the whole time he was there for the last 60% I think. <br /><br />There were a lot of new characters like Vida, Jude, Cole, and Nico. I really liked Vida a lot and all her sass. I totally ship her and Chubs together. I think they would be so cute together. She was so funny with her sarcastic comments. I loved Jude so much but I felt like despite the fact that he was 14/15 years old I pictured him more as a 12-year-old because compared to the other characters he was scared most of the time but then he did start to stand up and fight. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I CANNOT BELIEVE HE DIED LIKE WHYYYYY????!?!?!?!??! I LOVED HIM A LOT AND MY HEART BROKE AT THE END. WHY HIM AND NOT SOME OTHER CHARACTER!?!?! WHY HIM??!?!??! :( I'm going to miss him.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also really loved Cole and his personality. I feel like all these new characters were amazing and I liked them a lot. Although Zu sadly wasn’t in this book. <br /><br />I know I won't be reading the third book anytime soon and with that cliffhanger, I don't know what I'm going to do. I mean sure it's totally okay for an author to just leave their readers hanging. Absolutely fine. Now I have to wait until I can get my hands on the third book. This book was a big improvement from the first but I still love the first book. Also, I recently found out that THE DARKEST MINDS IS BECOMING A MOVIE AND I AM SO EXCITED FOR IT WHENEVER IT COMES OUT!!!!</span>

<div id="review_750144924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/750144924" />
    <a title="mich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17575003-mich"><img alt="mich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361178507p2/17575003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mich" href="/user/show/17575003-mich">mich</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=zzzzz">zzzzz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=main-character-is-lame">main-character-is-lame</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer750144924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5658471066993817353">In a word, disappointing.<br/><br/>I thought The Darkest Minds was awesome, I found the plot interesting and the supporting characters and their relationships with each other to be very well done. I had only 2 issues with that book -- the pacing and Ruby. Unfortunately, in this sequel, those 2 things still sucked and worse, the suckiness was actually magnified.<br/><br/>The thing is, I really liked how the first book ended. I didn’t like that it came about as a result of Ruby’s stupid decisions, and the cliffhanger</span>
  <span id="freeText5658471066993817353" style="display:none">In a word, disappointing.<br /><br />I thought The Darkest Minds was awesome, I found the plot interesting and the supporting characters and their relationships with each other to be very well done. I had only 2 issues with that book -- the pacing and Ruby. Unfortunately, in this sequel, those 2 things still sucked and worse, the suckiness was actually magnified.<br /><br />The thing is, I really liked how the first book ended. I didn’t like that it came about as a result of Ruby’s stupid decisions, and the cliffhanger itself came from her Worst Decision Ever <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[erasing Liam’s memory and aligning with the League <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but it sure did intrigue me and had me highly anticipating the sequel -- I thought it opened up all kinds of doors to the story and I was excited to see where the author would take it. <br /><br />Turns out, she didn’t take it anywhere interesting. This book dragged A LOT. It was just the same things happening over and over again, which made for a really boring and tedious read. The only reason I diligently kept pushing through was because I wanted to see what had become of Liam. I do love me a good emotional reunion and I was hoping to get something amazing here. Did I get it? Um, not quite. It was ok, but I was left wanting. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The way the whole memory thing with Liam played out ended up being kind of dumb. I did like how I was kept guessing for a bit about how things would work out with Ruby and him, but then...they kiss and then he just magically remembers everything? That’s it? Aww, how sweet. Actually, no, lame. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And then there’s Ruby.<br /><br />Ruby is more stupid than ever, to the point where I just can’t root for her anymore. Her decision making process is completely fucked up. The things she does MAKES NO SENSE. The worst thing about it is that she fails time and again to learn anything from her mistakes. <br /><br />And her pity parties, ugh, her damn pity parties! I was hoping my invitation got lost in the mail (seeing as I didn’t particularly enjoy myself at the ones she threw in the first book), but no, that hope was futile. The girl is still moaning on and on and wallowing about being a monster, blah blah blah. <br /><br />Some other thoughts:<br />Ruby and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Chubs <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> -- one of the few things I liked in this book was their relationship. His character gets some good development and his friendship with Ruby is done really well and feels authentic. <br />Ruby and Liam -- their relationship on the other hand, didn’t quite feel as believable. I thought their romance in book 1 was very sweet, but it wasn’t close to what this book tries to ram down your throat. Where the hell did this deep, deep soul love between Ruby and Liam come from? I for one, wasn’t convinced of it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also don’t get how Liam was able to forgive Ruby so quickly, especially, as he notes, she’s not even sorry for what she did. She was incredibly manipulative and completely took away his freedom to make the choice for himself. Why did she do that, because she knew better? Yeah, makes sense, seeing as she’s just <i>so</i> good at making smart decisions for herself, sure, she should do it for others too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />Vida and Jude -- like the supporting characters we met in the first book, these two were really nice additions. Bracken does a great job again of giving us a diverse and memorable supporting cast.<br /><br />Oh well, that's that I guess. I don’t think I care enough anymore about our main character Ruby to make a point of reading the next book. If I happen to come across it when it comes out, maybe I’ll check it out (if only to hopefully see Zu again). </span>
  <a data-text-id="5658471066993817353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982936383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3566693433349859254">Abso-freaking-lutely amazing. Go figure why it took me 8 months to read this. I don't even know why. I'd loved the first book and I guess delay after delay, I forgot about it entirely. A grave mistake because this is a swoon-worthy sequel that had me hyperventilating from page one to page.<br/><br/>In case you're not familiar with the plot, then let me hook you up. Some years before, a disease that targets children spread. Some died but some didn't. Those who didn't die have powers. The government with th</span>
  <span id="freeText3566693433349859254" style="display:none">Abso-freaking-lutely amazing. Go figure why it took me 8 months to read this. I don't even know why. I'd loved the first book and I guess delay after delay, I forgot about it entirely. A grave mistake because this is a swoon-worthy sequel that had me hyperventilating from page one to page.<br /><br />In case you're not familiar with the plot, then let me hook you up. Some years before, a disease that targets children spread. Some died but some didn't. Those who didn't die have powers. The government with the excuse of rehabilitation took those children from their parents and kept them in special facilities in order to keep them under control. <br /><br />In the first book, Ruby, as sixteen-year-old girl wanders about after breaking out from Thurmond (a rehabilitation facility) when she meets some kids from the League of Children, an organization leaded by a former politician, who wants to take down the current governor of the United States. Ruby is an Orange, meaning she can get inside people's head, see their memories, take control of them. In the first book she's not able to control her powers all that well which is why when she touches the hand of a member of the League of Children, she sees his memory of killing two children mercilessly because he thought they were worthless. She then runs away and comes across, Liam, Chubs and Zu and thus the adventure begins. <br /><br />Ruby has evolved so much in the sequel, it's impossible to think of her as that fragile, broken little girl she was when all of this began. Now, she's working with the League, and runs ops for them. But something is brewing inside the League, someone is trying to take control and do as they please with those they deem worthless. With the help of Jude and Vida, fellow LoC members, she must retrieve the lost usb stick that Liam's brother, Cole, lost. Liam is unaware of the existence of such a stick sewn inside the jacket, which he took from his last visit home, and was his brothers. So, that means Ruby has to search for Liam. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I feel like I'm losing my damn mind, like your face has been carved into my heart, and I don't remember when, and I don't understand why, but the scar is there, and I can't get it to heal. It won't go. I can't make it fade. And you won't even look at me.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Hence the name of fhe book: Never Fade <br /><br />Don't worry, there's lot of Chubs in this, I love the guy too. I promise you, you're going to love the new characters. Jude is really young and he's so protective it's kind of cute. Vida, well she's badass, and "bitch" is her favorite word, but you're gonna warm up to her.<br /><br />There are lots of twists, lots of unpredictable moments, and a cliffhanger in the end which accounts for an omg moment. Alexandra Bracken, despite her age, she's pretty brilliant when it comes to describing military procedures and writing amazing, action-packed scenes.<br /><br />If you liked the first book, then I don't doubt that you'll like this as much. In my case, I loved the first book and loved this book even more, because of the character development, and evolution of the world, that's been taken to a whole new level. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3566693433349859254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1092039830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1092039830" />
    <a title="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat"><img alt="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491529769p2/6759885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1092039830?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" href="/user/show/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat">Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat?shelf=signed-copy">signed-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1092039830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3493091961042289666"><a href='http://novelheartbeat.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419949228i/13149855.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Wow, you guys, just wow! Sometimes middle books have this thing called Second Book Syndrome – yeah, you know what I’m talking about – and you end up being totally disappointed. Such was NOT the case with this one! It was just as good as the first book. It blew me away!<br/><br/>As I mentioned in my review of the <i>In Time</i> novella, Alexandra’s prose is very engaging. She has a way with words! She’s also a pro at characterization. All of the characters felt so real. Actually, I kinda wish they were, so we</span>
  <span id="freeText3493091961042289666" style="display:none"><a href="http://novelheartbeat.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419949228i/13149855.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wow, you guys, just wow! Sometimes middle books have this thing called Second Book Syndrome – yeah, you know what I’m talking about – and you end up being totally disappointed. Such was NOT the case with this one! It was just as good as the first book. It blew me away!<br><br>As I mentioned in my review of the <i>In Time</i> novella, Alexandra’s prose is very engaging. She has a way with words! She’s also a pro at characterization. All of the characters felt so real. Actually, I kinda wish they were, so we could be friends in real life. I loved the characters just as much as I did in <i>The Darkest Minds</i>! Ruby! Liam! CHUBS! I love Chubs. I love him so much. He’s definitely my favorite character of this series!<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“I’m not the same person. I’m not, and I know that. I’m not okay with who I am or what I had to do, but I’m also not okay with us separating again! Don’t do that! Don’t just disappear! If you’re mad at me, then hit me or something – just don’t think that I don’t want to stay with you. I’ll always want to stay with you!”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>I LOVE HIM SO MUCH I CAN’T TAKE IT. Even when he was being an asshat, it was because he cared too much. He covers up fear and pain with anger, and sometimes takes things out on the wrong people. But underneath it all, it’s because he cares about them. He just wanted to protect them. And the best thing? There is no romance between Chubs and Ruby. It’s strictly platonic. I LOVE THIS. It’s so, SO rare to see relationships like that anymore! It was the <i>perfect</i> platonic best friend relationship. *hugs book to chest* (Also, I miss Zu!!)<br><br>Ruby is probably one of my favorite heroines I’ve ever read. She’s fiercely loyal to her friends and would do anything to protect them, even if it meant making the hard decision. Sacrificing something for them. It’s funny, because she didn’t view herself in a very positive light – actually, in this book she struggles a bit with the darkness inside of her. She thinks she’s a monster, and jokes about her “winning personality” – even her peers see her as a bit of an ice queen. But, I think she’s brave and selfless. She puts others above herself constantly, and deep down the most important thing to her is keeping her loved ones safe.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>I had something to accomplish and people to protect, and no one – especially not Rob Meadows – was going to keep me from it so long as there was breath in my body.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>I also enjoyed meeting the new characters! I really liked Jude. He was simple, and a bit clingy and okay, kind of annoying sometimes; but he had an innocence to him, and he was like a ball of sunshine. I swear, <i>nothing</i> got that kid down. It was endearing, though…I wanted to hug him! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I refuse to believe he is dead. I REFUSE. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And then there’s Vida. Oh, Vida…how do I feel about you? I still don’t really know. I’m not gonna lie, I wanted to knock her teeth out in the beginning. She was just so…<i>insufferable</i>. Good lord, she was awful. Like Chubs said, <i>she’d drive a saint to murder</i>. But then, suddenly, she wasn’t so bad anymore. She started looking out for Ruby and the gang, protecting them. It was clear that she started caring about them. And she started growing on me. (Like a fungus.) I started laughing at her horrible comments instead of being annoyed. She has a terrible sense of humor, I’ll say that, but the back and forth banter between her and the others was actually pretty amusing.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“You – you – I can’t -” Chubs sputtered, too furious to form an actual sentence. “Come out here. Right now!”<br>“Come and get me, big boy,” she sang back. “I know I don’t have the parts you like, but we can always make it work.”<br>“Oh, like a functioning brain?” he shouted.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“I’m trying to make up for the sleep I lost when you started screeching at each other like cats in heat.”<br>“Miss Vida,” Liam said, “has anyone ever told you that you are positively the whipped cream on the sundae of life?”<br>She glared at him. “Anyone ever told you your head is shaped like a pencil?”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>Another thing I loved about this book: I was 100% emotionally invested. I got a little misty sometimes at the <i>stupidest</i> things! (It’s kind of embarrassing, really.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was very surprised by how emotional I got when Ruby found Chubs! I didn’t realize how freaking much I’d missed him!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ALL THE FEELS, GUYS. Lots of warm fuzzies, lots of shocks, but also sorrow, I’m afraid. Ruby and Liam’s interactions were so heartbreaking. I hated the distance between them! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But I was SO glad that he got his memories back!! A little piece of my soul died when she wiped his memories in the first book. I was seriously hoping it was reversible, so yay! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There were so many times where I was holding my breath, frantically flipping the pages to find out what happened next. So much action – this book was explosive! There was never a dull moment. Even when there wasn’t anything happening (which was rare anyway), it was interesting.<br><br>Boy, does Alexandra Bracken know how to write an ending. I should have known, though, with the way both <i>Darkest Minds</i> and <i>In Time</i> ended. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I still want to know what the hell happened to Gabe!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’m almost afraid to read the last book!<br><br><b>Favorite quotes:</b><br><br><i>“Sometimes you’re the one speeding along in a panic, doing too much, not paying attention, wrecking things you don’t mean to. And sometimes life just happens to you, and you can’t dodge it. It crashes into you because it wants to see what you’re made of.”<br><br>“Life isn’t fair,” I said. “It’s taken me a while to get that. It’s always going to disappoint you in some way or another. You’ll make plans, and it’ll push you in another direction. You will love people, and they’ll be taken away no matter how hard you fight to keep them. You’ll try for something and won’t get it. You don’t have to find meaning in it; you don’t have to try to change things. You just have to accept the things that are out of your hands and try to take care of yourself.”</i><br><br><br><b>This review was originally posted on <a href="http://novelheartbeat.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Heartbeat</a>. To see a breakdown of my assessment, please visit the full review!</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5935625254647588767">DNFed at page 140.<br/><br/>I liked The Darkest Minds, but it's been about a year since I read it. I thought that I remembered how things ended, but I felt so lost getting into Never Fade. I couldn't connect to the new characters and didn't know why Ruby was... doing... whatever... she was doing?? See, I really don't know?<br/><br/>I have learned that I just do not mesh with Bracken's writing style. I think she has amazing premises but I always get lost in the descriptions. I've struggled through 3 of her books and</span>
  <span id="freeText5935625254647588767" style="display:none">DNFed at page 140.<br /><br />I liked The Darkest Minds, but it's been about a year since I read it. I thought that I remembered how things ended, but I felt so lost getting into Never Fade. I couldn't connect to the new characters and didn't know why Ruby was... doing... whatever... she was doing?? See, I really don't know?<br /><br />I have learned that I just do not mesh with Bracken's writing style. I think she has amazing premises but I always get lost in the descriptions. I've struggled through 3 of her books and even though I've liked 2, it was a pain to get through them. I'm not in the mood to slog through something right now. I even tried this one on audiobook to help boost me along, but it was even harder to focus with the audio. I'm frustrated because I own the whole trilogy, but I've had them for like 3 years now and I just don't care about them anymore. I'm going to leave Ruby's story as a standalone for the time being. I may return to this series in the future, but right now I'm too frustrated and disinterested to continue.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7585179866128925447">2 1/2 stars. Enjoyed this <i>a bit</i> more than the previous one.<br/><br/>Wow, surprisingly, this book wasn't some fucked up road trip!<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this one and imo it was a little better than the previous one. Many people said that the first one was the best in the series - which I hated - and the next two books are worse - I liked the second book better, so I have hope that the third book can work out for me. I will definitely be reading it after this horrible cliffhanger for an ending.<br/><br/>◇I definitely didn</span>
  <span id="freeText7585179866128925447" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. Enjoyed this <i>a bit</i> more than the previous one.<br /><br />Wow, surprisingly, this book wasn't some fucked up road trip!<br /><br />I really enjoyed this one and imo it was a little better than the previous one. Many people said that the first one was the best in the series - which I hated - and the next two books are worse - I liked the second book better, so I have hope that the third book can work out for me. I will definitely be reading it after this horrible cliffhanger for an ending.<br /><br />◇I definitely didn't expect Ruby to become a little stronger in this book. In the first book, she was a really weak heroine, always crying at small things and NOT kicking butt. However, in this book, she actually <b>doesn't</b> cry this much and there are small action scenes.<br /><br />◇The plot was better too. I feel like we have a <i>legit</i> story to read in this one. 3/4 of the book wasn't spent in a car (like the previous book) and there was some pretty sick dun dun dun's and twists. It was fun reading and I enjoyed it.<br /><br />※I just wish it wasn't so <i>long</i>. I was bored at some parts and skimmed a couple of pages and some parts in the book just didn't hold my interest.<br /><br />Overall, it was okay, but I just wished it wasn't so long and was a bit more exciting. </span>

<div id="review_3509205548" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3509205548" />
    <a title="Lisann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104031480-lisann"><img alt="Lisann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592343074p2/104031480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3509205548?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisann" href="/user/show/104031480-lisann">Lisann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104031480-lisann?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104031480-lisann?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3509205548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2123583799988730"><blockquote>
  <i>“Then he was stepping back, away, letting distance flood between us again. His voice was low, rough. "Give 'em hell, darlin'."<br/>"And for the love of God, bitch, don't get stabbed this time!" Vida added.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><u>
  <b>I LOVE THIS BOOK!</b>
</u> Okay after this <i>important</i> announcement we can now start the review.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531216880i/25949711._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='60' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/112231544-sunshine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sunshine</a><br/><br/><u>
  <b>The story:</b>
</u><br/><br/>At the beginning of the book there is a <b>time jump of six months</b> which I always like because it gives the characters the opportunity to have experiences without us havi</span>
  <span id="freeText2123583799988730" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Then he was stepping back, away, letting distance flood between us again. His voice was low, rough. "Give 'em hell, darlin'."<br>"And for the love of God, bitch, don't get stabbed this time!" Vida added.” </i>
</blockquote><br><u>
  <b>I LOVE THIS BOOK!</b>
</u> Okay after this <i>important</i> announcement we can now start the review.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531216880i/25949711._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="60" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/112231544-sunshine" rel="nofollow noopener">Sunshine</a><br><br><u>
  <b>The story:</b>
</u><br><br>At the beginning of the book there is a <b>time jump of six months</b> which I always like because it gives the characters the opportunity to have experiences without us having to accompany them all the time. According to an agreement at the end of the first book, <b>Ruby will be trained as an agent</b> during this time and will be prepared for various missions and crisis situations with her team consisting of <b>Vida</b> (thanks girl for adding some sass into this book), <b>Jude </b>and <b>Nico</b>. Ruby is no longer the naive girl who tries to keep her powers secret. She trains them within the six months to finally gain full control and to be able to interact with people without fear. Ruby is now so in control of her powers that <b>she is being used to interrogate people by entering their memories</b> and finding out what really happened in different situations. That's all I can tell you about the plot of the book, because everything else would spoiler too much.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“Oh, I'm sorry," Chubs said, 'apparently the middle of my sentence interrupted the beginning of yours. Do continue.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The characters:</u>
</b><br><br>In this book, Ruby goes through several <b>character developments</b> that I've wanted to see since the first book. I love reading the <i>darker sides</i> of characters because it just makes them more human. Ruby also likes to dive into <b>moral grey areas</b> which I always find great. There is nothing better than to see a protagonist grow from a broken child into a self-confident, courageous teenager who is committed to the well-being of her group and can keep a more or less cool head in crisis situations. The author manages to <b>emotionally bind me to all the side characters</b> from Ruby's team and her friends, which I was all the more enthusiastic about as they all met each other. Oh and to everyone who has already read this book: am I the only one <b>who ships Vida and Chubs</b>? I can see these two <i>slowly</i> starting to get friends and maybe something else?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598886937i/30041396._SX540_.png" width="500" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>My thoughts:</u>
</b><br><br><b>The end of the first book promised drama and heartache</b>. In addition to that there is a lot of <u>action and plot twists</u> in the second book that make it almost <i>impossible</i> to put the book down. Unfortunately I had to do exactly that because Sunshine and I agreed on reading 8 chapters in 2 days. <b>It was really hard to stop</b> because the tension is rising especially after the first third of the book.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“I don't want to just see someone's face; I want to know his shadow, too.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>The plot of the book just blew me away</b> and it was a huge step up from the first book! This story has exactly the right action moments where people get hurt, die and are kidnapped. The “<i>bad guys</i>” in this world are, as always, not the people with powers but <b>the society that does not accept people but wants to eliminate them, simply because they are different from the norm.</b> Therefore I think that their society has to change, or rather the politics which from the beginning made sure that everybody is afraid of their children and acted as if they were treated in camps for their own good. If someone would have been in power <u>who would have acted in the interest of the children</u> by offering them to train their powers, just to not endanger others. So much good could have come out of it!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1599303185i/30065599._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The only thing I don't love is the relationship between Liam and Ruby</b>. Don't get me wrong, I have nothing against Liam in general but he is just too nice for me. I would love to read about other kind of man but that is exactly the problem. There are no men and women here, but boys and girls. They are teenagers and so I can overlook the fact that my heart is not directly addressed in this book.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1599036519i/30049718.jpg" width="500" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I am <i>really</i> hyped for the third book and I can't wait to find out <b>what goes wrong next, who dies, who survives and how the political situation changes</b>. This series developed to be one of my favorites and I'm so really glad I've discovered it!<br><br>Special thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/101894427-joshita" rel="nofollow noopener">Joshita</a> for letting me steal her little images!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2123583799988730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer14496223137931651237"><i>Never Fade</i> was mind blowing. I've stared at my phone for so long trying to work out how to describe my feelings on the plot and the characters. My conclusion is I can honestly not write my feelings. I just loved this book. It didn't suffer from second book syndrome. I loved the characters. This book made me gasp, cry, laugh, and get mad along with the characters. That's all I can say, I don't know why I'm incapable of writing reviews for the books in this series -- especially considering I usual</span>
  <span id="freeText14496223137931651237" style="display:none"><i>Never Fade</i> was mind blowing. I've stared at my phone for so long trying to work out how to describe my feelings on the plot and the characters. My conclusion is I can honestly not write my feelings. I just loved this book. It didn't suffer from second book syndrome. I loved the characters. This book made me gasp, cry, laugh, and get mad along with the characters. That's all I can say, I don't know why I'm incapable of writing reviews for the books in this series -- especially considering I usually start my review while I'm reading the book so I can put my feelings as I come across them, but for some reason I can't. They're honestly purely amazing and all I can do is say read them right now!</span>

<div id="review_559491175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/559491175" />
    <a title="Bex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10552518-bex"><img alt="Bex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358302693p2/10552518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559491175?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bex" href="/user/show/10552518-bex">Bex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=bad-ass-heroines">bad-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=gory-as-hell">gory-as-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=kids-with-powers">kids-with-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=creepy-villains">creepy-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=pure-awesomeness-in-general">pure-awesomeness-in-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10552518-bex?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559491175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16685251965152651412">I will not be a bad person and ruin Never Fade, because that's not fair to Alexandra Bracken and all the anticipation she built and is still building leading up to the release of Never Fade, and also not fair to the people who actually don't like spoilers. (I have to say, I'm such a curious person that I sometimes look for spoilers. I know, it's a bad habit.)But also, WARNING. If you are really a spoiler-phobe you should keep away from this review and this page in general because I do glancingly</span>
  <span id="freeText16685251965152651412" style="display:none">I will not be a bad person and ruin Never Fade, because that's not fair to Alexandra Bracken and all the anticipation she built and is still building leading up to the release of Never Fade, and also not fair to the people who actually don't like spoilers. (I have to say, I'm such a curious person that I sometimes look for spoilers. I know, it's a bad habit.)But also, WARNING. If you are really a spoiler-phobe you should keep away from this review and this page in general because I do glancingly talk about some stuff in Never Fade, so...<br>Your choice. <br>But I promise I will tell you when said areas occur. <br><br>Let me turn your attention to the above, where I list the shelves this book is on, which are not spoilery so much as an indication of how much I actually enjoyed this book. I have a little rating system with my book shelves- at the bottom, there is the "very bad books" shelve, where you will find my one and two-star books. I have nothing for my three and four-stars, because they basically did not leave a huge impact on me, but my five-stars are divided into two shelves: the "favorites" and the "pure-awesomeness-in-general"s. Favorites were really, really good books, that I will treasure for the rest of my existence. Pure-awesomeness-in-generals are the ones I cry over when I think about them, the ones I will guard like some hyper-active mother bear, the ones I will chose time and time again to take with me on vacation even though I have a pile of unread books under the foot of my bed. <br><br>Obviously, this was one of those books. <br><br>I'm going to skip the part about how I teared up when I first saw the book at BEA and move on to something else now, because nobody really wants to hear about that. <br><br>And now I will spare you my obsession and get to the book because I have <b>A LOT</b> to say. Because of the last book, I was debating whether to wait a little while longer to read it in fear of another heart-gutting cliff hanger and waiting a year for the next one. To add to it, I was in the process of reading several other books, which I don't like to do. I feel like it's not proper reading hygiene or something. I was an agitated mess, and probably resembled a caged lion with all my pacing- though most of it had to be mental pacing because I was either in a train or a car most of the day. In short, I think I looked kind of like Emma Watson that one time:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413148ra/813081.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Except not really because I'm not Emma Watson and look nothing like her. Maybe if you made her shorter and more angsty...<br><br>When I opened it:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413148ra/813082.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/397251.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/581791.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Insert <b> WTF FACE </b> here. <br><br>M.U.F.M. MAJORLY UNEXPECTED FIT/MELTDOWN. Also the sound your face makes when it hits the pillow promptly thrown on it because of the M.U.F.M.<br><br>Ah, well, moving on from that little... episode, I went on from that bomb at the beginning to dive headfirst into Bracken's thought-provoking, descriptive, writing. <br><br>Questions that many people (including me) had/have about Never Fade:<br><br>~Will Ruby find Liam?<br>I am trusting you to use your common sense about what 512 pages could possibly be about.<br><br>~Will Clancy reappear? <br>Knowing Clancy, is that even a question?<br><br>~Is Liam's brother, Cole, making an appearance?<br>Yes... hee hee. <br><br>Okay, now book talk. <br>Never Fade was a brutal book. Not like the Gone or Maze Runner series where it honestly was not for people with delicate constitutions, but it was pretty harsh compared to the Darkest Minds. I'm talking about getting ready for gunshots and stab wounds and a whole-freaking-butt-load of some brain-blowing mind control. We already saw Ruby evolve tremendously as a character in the Darkest Minds, but if it's possible, she changed even more. <br>Such a badass heroine. <br><br>Since we're on the topic of characters, let's do some in-depth:<br>~Ruby. As I said before, she has some new found ass-kicking skills that come in handy throughout the book, and is way more ruthless than she ever was in the Darkest Minds. She has some soul-searching moments, some badass moments, some very tender moments between herself and a new character, Jude, who has quickly become one of my favorite characters. She's fiercely protective of all her friends, new and old, and I'm happy to say that my opinion of her being one of the best female protagonists I've ever read hasn't changed. <br><br>~Jude. I mentioned him already. If you haven't read the Darkest Minds, I'm telling you to leave right now because SPOILERS. Anyhoo, Jude is part of Ruby's team in the Children's League, who she views as naive and in need of protection. Jude's fourteen, even though he could pass for twelve, and is a trained yellow. He's open, willing to trust, and while to Ruby these seem like things that could get him killed, he has a flare for seeing the reasons why people do what they do. He also affectionately calls Ruby 'Roo', which I find adorable.<br><br>~Vida. Those of you who read chapter one already (up on Alexandra Bracken's blog) know that Vida has quite the potty mouth, which I honestly find refreshing. Actually, the amount of f-bombs dropped in Never Fade is refreshing, because who on earth with a full vocabulary of cuss words would be able to keep them inside while everything went to shit around them? Unless you are either really Christian or have extremely strict morals, which is kind of what the YA genre is kind of implying-but-not-really with the low level of cursing, I don't know how anyone expects to portray an accurate teenager. Vida has blue hair, is actually a blue, and throws herself into everything she does. She's hostile towards Ruby at first, feeling replaced, but she soon realizes that Ruby isn't so different from her. I also ship Vida+Chubs. <br><br><b> MINOR SPOILER AHEAD </b><br><br>~Cole. Elder brother of Liam, mentioned in the first book. He is important, but doesn't stick around for the bulk of the book. Frankly, he's an an ass sometimes, and though he cares about Liam, he doesn't really like people to know. I would say more, but... spoilers. <br><br><b> THE DANGER HAS PASSED, oh no, wait, MORE AHEAD! </b><br><br>Rest assured, this isn't all the characters in the book who play a major role. Among those who are returning from the Darkest Minds are: Cate,Rob,and Olivia, new ones are: Alban, Jarvin, and Knox. Oh, and there is at least one member of the Black Betty crew (Liam, Chubs, Zu, Ruby) other than Ruby in the book, though whether their stay is short or long I shall not say...<br><br><b> THIS TIME THE DANGER HAS ACTUALLY PASSED! YAY! </b><br><br>Tee Hee.<br><br>Never Fade has a ton of twists and turns, most of them are entirely unexpected, so be prepared with tissues and don't read it while eating anything you could choke on. <br><br>The ending:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/582264.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On an interesting side note: has anyone noticed that Ruby's initials spell out RED? Well, Alexandra Bracken actually answered that question, saying that all the oranges in TDM series have names relating to the color red, indicating that Oranges are actually more powerful than reds even though the government says otherwise. For example, Ruby's initials are RED, as said before, and Martin's name is similar to Mars, the red planet and the Roman god of war. She said we have to figure out Clancy's on our own, and I'm almost convinced that his initials CG, are for the chemical choking agent,CG, which is destroyed by water and is basically bad news for anyone not armed with a spray gun. <br><br>Thoughts?<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16685251965152651412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2549941593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2549941593" />
    <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52207144"><img alt="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568965358p2/52207144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2549941593?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" href="/user/show/52207144">♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781423187028" href="/book/show/18337328-never-fade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=finished-buddy-read">finished-buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=dystopia-and-utopian">dystopia-and-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=2018-reading-challenge">2018-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2549941593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5581006538317470527"><b><u>3 No regret ★'s</u> <br/><br/><i>I used to dream about turning back time, about reclaiming the things I’d lost and the person I used to be. But not anymore.</i></b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538948434i/26414769._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/53968639-nancy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nancy</a></b><br/><br/><i>Never Fade</i> was certainly better than <i>The Darkest Minds</i> but it still fell a bit flat to me. The first half dragged on and on and really it was kinda boring, then it would go really fast at others. It did make up for it in the last half but damn that was a lot of pages to get through in order for it to hold my attention. But once it did I w</span>
  <span id="freeText5581006538317470527" style="display:none"><b><u>3 No regret ★'s</u> <br><br><i>I used to dream about turning back time, about reclaiming the things I’d lost and the person I used to be. But not anymore.</i></b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538948434i/26414769._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/53968639-nancy" rel="nofollow noopener">Nancy</a></b><br><br><i>Never Fade</i> was certainly better than <i>The Darkest Minds</i> but it still fell a bit flat to me. The first half dragged on and on and really it was kinda boring, then it would go really fast at others. It did make up for it in the last half but damn that was a lot of pages to get through in order for it to hold my attention. But once it did I was hooked. There were a lot fewer plot holes and much better descriptions this time, so that's a plus. The characters are still great though and we meet some new friends. I love this ragtag group of characters :) Ruby has joined with the Children's Leauge and that is where we meet Vida (blue), Jude (yellow) and Nico (green). These three are a wonderful addition. <br><br><b>
  <u>Colors and their associated abilities:</u>
</b> <br><b>Green -</b> Photographic Memory<br><b>Blue -</b> Telekinesis <br><b>Yellow -</b> Electricity <br><b>Orange -</b> Mindfuckery<br><b>Red -</b> Fire<br><br><i>
  <b>“And people like you are the reason we have middle fingers.”</b>
</i><br><br><b>-Vida</b> is bloody fantastic, her personality alone made this book that much better. She is witty, sarcastic as hell, inappropriate and almost everything that comes out of her mouth is offensive in one way or another, she's also very guarded and doesn't show her emotions easily. Vida is <i>"positively the whipped cream on the sundae of life."</i> Just ask Liam :D <br><br><i>
  <b>“Apparently the middle of my sentence interrupted the beginning of yours. Do continue.”</b>
</i><br><br><b>-Chubs</b> is still one of my favorites. I was so excited when he came back into the picture. He never ever fails at making me laugh. Chubs can be a moody guy at times and he's also a bit of a control freak but Chubs is also brilliant, funny, trusting and extremely loyal. He makes one hell of a good friend! <br>*I sooo ship ♥Chubs and Vida♥! I ship them very very much!!! They'd be perfect together and really they could both use a little love in their lives.* <br><br><i>
  <b>“I don't want to just see someone's face; I want to know his shadow, too.”</b>
</i><br><br>Oh, <b>-Jude</b>... I abso-freakin-lutely love this strange kid. He just melted my heart and turned it into putty. He was so sweet and funny and boisterous. He was also magnetic and you couldn't help but have this fondness for the kid. Jude was one of the main reasons the first half didn't completely suck! <br><br><i>
  <b>“If a heart could break once, it shouldn't have been able to happen again.” </b>
</i><br><br><b>-Ruby</b>'s character has improved immensely since <i>The Darkest Minds</i>. I really like that her character keeps growing and maturing throughout this series. I love her kickass attitude and the protectiveness she has over her friends. She doesn't always make good decisions but that's life. We live and we learn. <br><i>
  <b>“I missed him. I missed him, I missed him -oh my God, I missed him so much.”</b>
</i><br><br>*Ruby is trying to find a way out of the Children's League when she learns that there is a divide between the agents - there are those who want to help the kids with powers and generally care about them and then those wanting them <b>ALL</b> dead. Rubby sets out on a secret mission with Jude and later Vida and Chubs join the search to find Liam. Who <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[doesn't know he has the flash drive with sensitive information. Information that could initially close the camps and allow the nation to rebuild. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>and so... Road Trip anyone?</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1539649118ra/26454213.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>“Give 'em hell, darlin”</b>
</i><br><br><b>-Liam</b> is still my everything! Gods I missed him so much. I even held a little grudge at Ruby for well you know. Liam was so lost and felt like something was missing and nothing was making any sense. His mind was all muddled up and unclear. The moment Liam came into the book, that was the point in which I was hooked. His personality is entrancing and he just has this charismatic way about him. He just lures you into his web and you're a goner. He's just so charming, compassionate brave and loyal.<br>*I still very much ship ♥Ruby and Liam♥. I love them together and they have such chemistry between them its almost tangible.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Goddammit, you stupid kid! You scared the shit out of me!”</i>
</b><br><br><b>-Cole</b> was just perfect! I love Liam's brother. It was nice getting to know him better and like Liam, it was impossible not to like the guy. Also, Cole is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a freaking RED <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!! I should have guessed this. I mean all the clues were there but I was completely surprised! I can't wait for more Cole :D<br><br><b>
  <i>“You all can thank me when you can still fight back. I saved us.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>-Clancy</b> is BACK! I really do like to hate this asshat. He's cunning, manipulative, untrustworthy and a complete freaking psychopath!!! But still, he knows how to keep it interesting that's for sure. <br><br>*The world <i>Bracken</i> has created has so much potential but sadly I'm just not loving it like I thought I would. I will be continuing with this series though and I am excited to see what happens next! That ending though, OMG it broke my heart into a million little pieces. Okie Dokie on to <i>In The Afterlight</i>.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Later, gator." <br>"In an hour, sunflower.”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538948434i/26414769._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1539652708ra/26454563.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538948434i/26414769._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“I think I'm losing it—I don't know what's happening, what happened, but I look at you, I look at you, and I love you so much. Not because of anything you've said, or done, or anything at all. I look at you, and I just love you, and it terrifies me. It terrifies me what I would do for you.”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1539652708ra/26454562.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“Don’t to that! Don’t just disappear! If you’re mad at me, then hit me or something-just don’t think that I don’t want to stay with you. I’ll always want to stay with you!”</i>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
